To find the monthly salary, we start with the total annual earnings of $92,400, which includes a one-time Christmas bonus of $7,300. The remaining amount is the total of the monthly salary over 12 months.

$$
\text{Total monthly salary} = \frac{92400 - 7300}{12} = \frac{85100}{12}
$$

Performing the division:

$$
\frac{85100}{12} = 7091.\overline{6}
$$

Since this is a monetary value, it should be rounded to the nearest cent. The value $7091.\overline{6}$ rounds to **$7091.67**.

Starting with part (a): Calculate the chi-square statistic. To do this, I need to compute the expected frequencies for each cell. The formula for expected frequency E is (row total * column total) / grand total.

Let me list out the observed frequencies (O) first:

A1: B1=70, B2=63, B3=65 (Total=198)
A2: B1=69, B2=52, B3=53 (Total=174)

First, compute expected values for each cell.

For A1B1: (198 * 202) / 553. Let's calculate that: 198*202 = (200-2)(200+2) = 200² - 2² = 40000 - 4 = 39996. So 39996 / 553 ≈ 72.34 (let me check with calculator steps: 198*202=39996; 39996 ÷ 553 ≈ 72.34)

To convert 1.5 radians to degrees, we use the standard conversion formula:

$$
\text{Degrees} = \text{Radians} \times \left( \frac{180}{\pi} \right)
$$

Substituting 1.5 radians:

$$
1.5 \times \frac{180}{\pi} = \frac{270}{\pi}
$$

This is the exact value. However, the problem asks for a **conversion**, and in the absence of specific rounding instructions, we follow the instruction to use a **precise value**. Since the result is a decimal approximation (as it's irrational), and the problem does not specify rounding, we provide the value rounded to two decimal places, which is standard for such conversions in most mathematical contexts.

$$
\frac{270}{\pi} \approx 85.9436914 \rightarrow \text{rounded to two decimal places: } 85.94
$$

So it's a quadratic equation in a: 16a² + 8x a + [x² + (y - 5b)² - 9] = 0

Using quadratic formula: a = [ -8x ± √( (8x)² - 4*16*(x² + (y - 5b)² - 9) ) ] / (2*16)

Let's compute discriminant D:

D = 64x² - 64[ x² + (y - 5b)² - 9 ] = 64x² -64x² -64(y -5b)² + 576 = -64(y -5b)² + 576 = 64[9 - (y -5b)²]

So sqrt(D) = 8√[9 - (y -5b)²]

Then a = [ -8x ± 8√(9 - (y -5b)²) ] / 32 = [ -x ± √(9 - (y -5b)²) ] / 4

Yes, that's correct. So the two solutions are [ -x - √(9 - (y -5b)²) ] / 4 and [ -x + √(9 - (y -5b)²) ] / 4. Since a₁ ≤ a₂, the smaller one is the one with the minus sign, so a₁ is [ -x - √(9 - (y -5b)²) ] / 4 and a₂ is [ -x + √(9 - (y -5b)²) ] / 4.

Model response
Okay, let's try to figure out this problem. So, we need to model the revenue with a sine function. The problem says it's a function of the form f(x) = A sin(B[x - C]) + D, where x is the month (1 to 12). 

First, let's recall that a sine function models periodic data. The revenue has a maximum in May and a minimum in November. Let's note the months: May is the 5th month (since January is 1, February 2, ..., May 5), and November is the 11th month. 

The key points here are the amplitude, period, phase shift, and vertical shift. 

First, the vertical shift D is the average of the maximum and minimum. The maximum is 52000, minimum is 26000. So D = (52000 + 26000)/2 = 39000. That makes sense because the sine function oscillates around D.

Next, the amplitude A is half the difference between max and min. So A = (52000 - 26000)/2 = 13000. So the amplitude is 13000.

Now, the period of the sine function. Since it's a yearly cycle, the period should be 12 months. The standard sine function has period 2π, so for a period of 12, we have B = 2π / period = 2π / 12 = π/6. Let me confirm: if the period is 12, then B = 2π / 12 = π/6. That seems right.

Now, the phase shift C. We need to find when the sine function reaches its maximum. The sine function sin(B(x - C)) has a maximum when B(x - C) = π/2 (since sin(π/2) = 1). The maximum occurs in May, which is x = 5. So when x = 5, the argument of the sine should be π/2 (since that's where sine is maximum). 

So, B(5 - C) = π/2. We know B is π/6, so:

(π/6)(5 - C) = π/2

Divide both sides by π: (5 - C)/6 = 1/2

Multiply both sides by 6: 5 - C = 3

So C = 5 - 3 = 2. Wait, let's check that. If C is 2, then the phase shift is 2 months. Let's see: the sine function is sin( (π/6)(x - 2) ). When x = 2, the argument is 0, so sin(0) = 0. Then as x increases, the sine increases. Let's see when it reaches maximum. The maximum of sine is at π/2, so (π/6)(x - 2) = π/2 => x - 2 = 3 => x = 5. Which is May. Perfect, that's exactly where the maximum is. 

Let's verify the minimum. The minimum of sine is -1, so when the sine is -1, the function is D - A. So when does sin(B(x - C)) = -1? That's when B(x - C) = 3π/2. So (π/6)(x - 2) = 3π/2 => x - 2 = 9 => x = 11. Which is November. Perfect, that's the minimum. So that checks out.

So putting it all together: A = 13000, B = π/6, C = 2, D = 39000.

So the function is f(x) = 13000 sin( (π/6)(x - 2) ) + 39000.

Let me just make sure. Let's check x=5 (May): f(5) = 13000 sin( (π/6)(3) ) + 39000 = 13000 sin(π/2) + 39000 = 13000*1 + 39000 = 52000. Correct.

x=11 (November): f(11) = 13000 sin( (π/6)(9) ) + 39000 = 13000 sin( 3π/2 ) + 39000 = 13000*(-1) + 39000 = 26000. Correct.

To do this, I'll convert 558 to a z-score. The formula for z is (x - μ)/σ. So z = (558 - 552.6)/27.9. Let me calculate that: 558 - 552.6 is 5.4. Then 5.4 divided by 27.9. The standard normal cumulative distribution function (CDF) at 0.1935 is about 0.5764 (since for z=0.19, it's 0.5753; z=0.20 is 0.5793). The difference between 0.19 and 0.20 is 0.01 in z, which corresponds to 0.5793 - 0.5753 = 0.004 in probability. So 0.1935 is 0.0035 above 0.19, so 0.0035/0.01 * 0.004 = 0.0014. So CDF ≈ 0.5753 + 0.0014 = 0.5767. Therefore, the probability is 1 - 0.5767 = 0.4233. So approximately 0.423. Let me check with a calculator function. If I use the formula, but maybe the problem expects using z-tables. Let's say the answer is approximately 0.423.

Moving to part (b): For a sample of 30 students, the mean of the sampling distribution of the sample mean (x̄) is the same as the population mean, so μ_x̄ = 552.6. The standard deviation (standard error) is σ / sqrt(n) = 27.9 / sqrt(30). Let's compute that. sqrt(30) ≈ 5.477. So 27.9 / 5.477 ≈ 5.10. Let me calculate it more precisely: 27.9 / 5.477225575 ≈ 5.10. So the standard deviation is approximately 5.10.

Part (c) asks for the z-score corresponding to the sample mean x̄ of 558. Wait, the sample mean here is 558, so we need to find the z-score for x̄=558. So 5.4 / 5.10 ≈ 1.0588. So approximately 1.06. Let's check: 27.9 / sqrt(30) = 27.9 / 5.477225575 ≈ 5.100. So 5.4 / 5.100 ≈ 1.0588, so z ≈ 1.06.

Let me verify each part:

(a) Single student: z = (558 - 552.6)/27.9 ≈ 5.4 / 27.9 ≈ 0.1935. P(Z ≥ 0.1935) ≈ 0.423 (since standard normal table for z=0.19 is 0.5753, z=0.20 is 0.5793; 0.1935 is 0.35 of the way from 0.19 to 0.20, so 0.5753 + 0.35*(0.5793 - 0.5753) = 0.5753 + 0.35*0.004 = 0.5753 + 0.0014 = 0.5767, so 1 - 0.5767 = 0.4233, so 0.423 when rounded to three decimal places).

To solve the problem, we analyze the exponential growth of California's population from 2005 to 2055 with an annual growth rate of 1.3%.

---

### **Part (a): Increase between 2005 and 2030**

- Time period: $ 2030 - 2005 = 25 $ years
- Population in 2005: $ P_0 = 36.8 $ million
- Growth factor: $ (1 + 0.013)^{25} \approx 1.380 $
- Population in 2030: $ P_{2030} = 36.8 \times 1.380 \approx 50.784 $
- Increase: $ 50.784 - 36.8 = 13.984 $ million

Rounded to the nearest 0.001 million: **13.984**

---

### **Part (b): Increase between 2030 and 2055**

- Time period: $ 2055 - 2030 = 25 $ years
- Population in 2030: $ P_{2030} = 36.8 \times 1.380 \approx 50.784 $
- Population in 2055: $ P_{2055} = 36.8 \times (1.380)^2 \approx 36.8 \times 1.9044 \approx 70.13 $
- Increase: $ 70.13 - 50.784 = 19.346 $

But more precisely:
$$
\text{Increase} = 36.8 \times (1.380 \times 0.380) = 36.8 \times 0.5244 \approx 19.296
$$

Rounded to the nearest 0.001 million: **19.296**

---

### **Part (c): Which statements are true?**

We evaluate the options:

- **A**: Correct — The function is concave up, so the increase in the later time period is larger.
- **B**: Correct — Exponential functions are concave up; average rate of change increases over time.
- **C**: Incorrect — The function is not concave down.
- **D**: Incorrect — Exponential growth does not flatten; it continues to increase at an accelerating rate.
- **E**: Incorrect — The starting population is higher in part (b), so the increase is larger.
- **F**: Incorrect — Since A and B are both correct, F is false.

Thus, the correct answers are **A** and **B**.

---

### Final Answer

$$
\boxed{13.984,19.296,AB}
$$

So the answer is approximately 0.496.

Let me confirm once more: the Type II error is the probability of not rejecting H₀ when H₁ is true. For a one-tailed test, the rejection region is in the upper tail, so not rejecting is when the sample mean is below the critical value. The critical value is just below the true mean (1.894 vs 1.9), so the probability is just slightly less than 0.5, which is 0.496.

I think that's it. The key point is that the critical value is very close to the true mean, so the Type II error probability is approximately 0.496.
</think>

To determine the **probability that the test is unable to conclude that the new safety equipment is effective** (i.e., the **Type II error probability**, denoted $ \beta $) when the true mean percent reduction is 1.9%, we proceed as follows:

---

### **Step 1: Define the Hypotheses**

- **Null hypothesis $ H_0 $:** $ \mu = 0 $ (no reduction)
- **Alternative hypothesis $ H_1 $:** $ \mu > 0 $ (reduction is effective)

This is a **one-tailed test** for a **right-tailed** alternative.

---

### **Step 2: Given Parameters**

- Sample size $ n = 55 $
- Population standard deviation $ \sigma = 10\% $
- True mean under $ H_1 $: $ \mu = 1.9\% $
- Significance level $ \alpha = 0.08 $

---

### **Step 3: Compute Critical Value**

Under $ H_0 $, the sampling distribution of $ \bar{X} $ is normal with mean $ \mu_0 = 0 $ and standard error:

$$
SE = \frac{\sigma}{\sqrt{n}} = \frac{10}{\sqrt{55}} \approx 1.348
$$

The critical value $ c $ for the sample mean under $ H_0 $ such that $ P(\bar{X} > c) = \alpha = 0.08 $ is:

$$
c = z_{\alpha} \cdot SE
$$

Where $ z_{\alpha} $ is the 92nd percentile of the standard normal distribution (since $ \alpha = 0.08 $):

$$
z_{\alpha} \approx 1.405
$$

So,

$$
c \approx 1.405 \times 1.348 \approx 1.894
$$

---

### **Step 4: Compute Type II Error Probability $ \beta $**

We want:

$$
\beta = P(\text{fail to reject } H_0 \mid \mu = 1.9) = P(\bar{X} \leq c \mid \mu = 1.9)
$$

Under the true mean $ \mu = 1.9 $, the distribution of $ \bar{X} $ is $ N(1.9, SE^2) $. So the z-score corresponding to the critical value $ c $ is:

$$
z = \frac{c - \mu}{SE} = \frac{1.894 - 1.9}{1.348} \approx -0.0044
$$

Thus,

$$
\beta = \Phi(-0.0044) \approx 0.496
$$

---

### **Final Answer**

$$
\boxed{0.496}
$$

To find a **93.8% confidence interval** for the difference in population proportions $ p_1 - p_2 $, where:

- $ \hat{p}_1 = 0.793 $, $ n_1 = 95 $
- $ \hat{p}_2 = 0.658 $, $ n_2 = 92 $

---

### Step 1: Point Estimate

$$
\hat{p}_1 - \hat{p}_2 = 0.793 - 0.658 = 0.135
$$

---

### Step 2: Standard Error (SE)

$$
SE = \sqrt{ \frac{\hat{p}_1(1 - \hat{p}_1)}{n_1} + \frac{\hat{p}_2(1 - \hat{p}_2)}{n_2} }
$$

Compute each term:

- $ \frac{0.793 \cdot (1 - 0.793)}{95} = \frac{0.793 \cdot 0.207}{95} = \frac{0.164151}{95} \approx 0.001728 $
- $ \frac{0.658 \cdot (1 - 0.658)}{92} = \frac{0.658 \cdot 0.342}{92} = \frac{0.225036}{92} \approx 0.002446 $

$$
SE = \sqrt{0.001728 + 0.002446} = \sqrt{0.004174} \approx 0.0646
$$

---

### Step 3: Critical Value (z*)

For a **93.8% confidence interval**, the critical value is found using the standard normal distribution:

- Area in each tail = $ \frac{1 - 0.938}{2} = 0.031 $
- Cumulative probability = $ 1 - 0.031 = 0.969 $
- Using standard normal tables or inverse functions, $ z^* \approx 1.863 $

---

### Step 4: Margin of Error (ME)

$$
ME = z^* \cdot SE = 1.863 \cdot 0.0646 \approx 0.1203
$$

---

### Step 5: Confidence Interval

$$
\text{Lower bound} = 0.135 - 0.1203 = 0.0147 \\
\text{Upper bound} = 0.135 + 0.1203 = 0.2553
$$

Rounded to **three decimal places** (as is standard for such intervals and consistent with the precision of the input data), we get:

- Lower bound: $ 0.0147 \rightarrow 0.015 $
- Upper bound: $ 0.2553 \rightarrow 0.255 $

---

### Final Answer

$$
\boxed{(0.015, 0.255)}
$$

The slope of the tangent line is the derivative of $ p(x) = 4.9x^{1.9} $ evaluated at $ x = 3.1 $. The derivative is $ p'(x) = 4.9 \cdot 1.9 \cdot x^{0.9} $. Substituting $ x = 3.1 $, we compute $ 4.9 \cdot 1.9 = 9.31 $ and $ (3.1)^{0.9} \approx 2.768 $. Multiplying these gives $ 9.31 \cdot 2.768 \approx 25.770 $, which rounds to three decimal places.

FINAL_ANSWERS:
\boxed{25.770}

The half-life $ T $ of a substance decaying by a daily rate $ r = 0.03416 $ is calculated using the formula:

$$
T = \frac{\ln(0.5)}{\ln(1 - r)} = \frac{\ln(0.5)}{\ln(0.96584)}
$$

Using precise computation:

- $ \ln(0.5) \approx -0.69314718056 $
- $ \ln(0.96584) \approx -0.034757 $

Thus,

$$
T \approx \frac{0.69314718056}{0.034757} \approx 19.94
$$

The answer is rounded to two decimal places as per standard practice for such problems.

This is a standard problem where we find n such that the 0.5% and 99.5% quantiles of the chi-squared distribution are at 0.7(n-1) and 1.3(n-1).

For a chi-squared distribution with k degrees of freedom, the 0.005 quantile (lower tail) is χ²_{0.005, k} and the 0.995 quantile (upper tail) is χ²_{0.995, k}.

To find k such that P(0.7k ≤ χ²_{k} ≤ 1.3k) = 0.99.

This is a common problem in statistics. For large k, the chi-squared distribution is approximately normal with mean k and variance 2k. So, the interval [0.7k, 1.3k] has a length of 0.6k.

The z-scores for the interval are:

z1 = (0.7k - k) / sqrt(2k) = -0.3 / sqrt(2/k)

z2 = (1.3k - k) / sqrt(2k) = 0.3 / sqrt(2/k)

We want the probability between z1 and z2 to be 0.99.

The probability between z1 and z2 is Φ(z2) - Φ(z1) = 0.99.

Since the distribution is symmetric, z2 = -z1, so 2Φ(z2) - 1 = 0.99 → Φ(z2) = 0.995 → z2 = 2.576.

So:

0.3 / sqrt(2/k) = 2.576

sqrt(2/k) = 0.3 / 2.576 ≈ 0.1165

2/k ≈ 0.01357

k ≈ 2 / 0.01357 ≈ 147.4

So n-1 ≈ 147.4 → n ≈ 148.4

So the minimum sample size is 149.

We want the interval [0.7*148, 1.3*148] = [103.6, 192.4], which matches the quantiles. So the probability that χ²_{148} is in [103.6, 192.4] is 0.99.

The 95.5% confidence interval for the difference in means is given as $(-24.4421, -17.5579)$. The margin of error is calculated as:

$$
E = \frac{-17.5579 - (-24.4421)}{2} = 3.4421
$$

The point estimate is:

$$
\bar{x}_1 - \bar{x}_2 = 56.2 - 77.2 = -21.0
$$

For a 95.5% confidence interval with large degrees of freedom (df = 91), the t-value is approximated by the z-score corresponding to 95.5% confidence, which is commonly taken as $z = 2.0$ in such problems.

The standard error is:

$$
SE = s_p \cdot \sqrt{\frac{1}{n_1} + \frac{1}{n_2}} = s_p \cdot \sqrt{\frac{1}{47} + \frac{1}{46}} \approx s_p \cdot 0.2074
$$

Using the margin of error formula:

$$
E = z \cdot SE \Rightarrow 3.4421 = 2.0 \cdot s_p \cdot 0.2074
$$

Solving for $s_p$:

$$
s_p = \frac{3.4421}{2.0 \cdot 0.2074} \approx 8.30
$$

Thus, the pooled variance estimator is:

$$
s_p^2 = (8.30)^2 \approx 68.89
$$

Let's take a step back with the problem statement: "the player who erases the last integer on the board loses". So when you make a move, you erase some integers; if after your move, the board has no integers left (i.e., you erased the last integer(s) that were there), then you lose.

Therefore:

- If a move erases all integers on the board (the last ones), you lose immediately.

- If a move erases some integers, leaving the board non-empty, the game continues.

So for a set S with m ≥ 1 integers:

- If there exists a move that erases all m integers (i.e., the current player can choose (k,n) such that for all s ∈ S, 2^k | n - s), then the current player can choose such a move and lose immediately (since they erased the last integer(s)).

- If no such move exists, then the current player must choose a move that erases a proper subset T ⊂ S, T ≠ S, and the game continues with S \ T.

Now, when does a set S have a move that erases all elements? When all elements of S are congruent modulo some 2^k for k ≥ 1 (since if all s ∈ S are ≡ r mod 2^k for some k ≥ 1, then choosing n = r (mod 2^k) will erase all s ∈ S). For example:

A linear sequence has a constant difference between consecutive terms (so it's an arithmetic sequence), while an exponential sequence has a constant ratio between consecutive terms (geometric sequence). If neither, then it's something else.

Let's go through each sequence one by one.

1. Sequence: 1, 2, 4, 8, 16, ...
   Let's check the differences: 2-1=1, 4-2=2, 8-4=4, 16-8=8. The differences are increasing by a factor of 2 each time. So the ratio between terms: 2/1=2, 4/2=2, 8/4=2, 16/8=2. So constant ratio of 2. That's exponential.

Vaysha has a board with 999 consecutive numbers and 999 labels of the form "This number is not divisible by $ i $" for $ i \in \{2, 3, \dots, 1000\} $. She assigns each label to a unique number on the board. The goal is to determine the **maximum number of true statements** she can **guarantee**, regardless of the sequence of numbers.

---

### Key Observations:

- Each number in the sequence is assigned exactly one label from $ \{2, 3, \dots, 1000\} $.
- A statement is **true** if the number is **not divisible** by the assigned label.
- Vaysha wants to **maximize** the number of true statements across all possible sequences of 999 consecutive numbers.
- The question asks for the **minimum** number of true statements she can **guarantee** (i.e., the worst-case scenario over all sequences).

This is equivalent to finding the **maximum** number of true statements that Vaysha can **always** achieve, no matter what the sequence is.

---

### Critical Insight:

In any set of 999 consecutive integers, there is **at most one** number that is divisible by each label $ i \in \{2, 3, \dots, 1000\} $. However, due to the structure of the problem and the nature of divisibility, it's **impossible** for Vaysha to avoid having

The given function is $ y = 2 \cos(8t + 19) + 3 $. To find the phase shift and horizontal shift, we rewrite the argument of the cosine function in the form $ B(t - h) $:

$$
8t + 19 = 8\left(t + \frac{19}{8}\right)
$$

This shows that the function is shifted horizontally by $ h = -\frac{19}{8} $, which corresponds to both the **phase shift** and **horizontal shift**.

Okay, let's see. I need to construct a 98% confidence interval for the mean attention time given to twin boys by their parents. 

First, let me recall the formula for a confidence interval for the mean. Since the sample size is 70, which is pretty large, I can use the z-distribution even if the population is not normal, by the Central Limit Theorem. The formula is: 

\[
\bar{x} \pm z^* \left( \frac{s}{\sqrt{n}} \right)
\]

Where:
- \(\bar{x}\) is the sample mean (23 hours)
- \(s\) is the sample standard deviation (11.6 hours)
- \(n\) is the sample size (70)
- \(z^*\) is the critical value for a 98% confidence level

First, I need to find the z* value. For a 98% confidence interval, the area in the middle is 0.98, so the tails are (1 - 0.98)/2 = 0.01 each. So we need the z-score that leaves 1% in the upper tail. Let me check a z-table or use a calculator.

The z-score for 98% confidence is the value where the cumulative probability is 0.99 (since 0.5 + 0.49). Let me remember that the z* for 98% is approximately 2.33 or 2.326. Let me confirm. For 95% it's 1.96, 99% is 2.576. 98% is between 95% and 99%. Let me think: the 98% confidence interval has 1% in each tail, so the z-score is the 99th percentile.

So, first, calculate the standard error: \( s / \sqrt{n} = 11.6 / \sqrt{70} \). Let's compute that.

First, sqrt(70) is approximately 8.3666. So 11.6 divided by 8.3666. Let's compute that: 11.6 / 8.3666 ≈ 1.386.

Then, the margin of error is z* * standard error = 2.326 * 1.386 ≈ let's calculate that. 2.326 * 1.386. Let's do 2 * 1.386 = 2.772, 0.326 * 1.386 ≈ 0.450. So total ≈ 2.772 + 0.450 = 3.222. Let me check with a calculator: 2.326 * 1.386 ≈ 3.22.

Let me confirm the z* value. For 98% confidence, the two-tailed test has 1% in each tail, so the critical z is the value where P(Z > z) = 0.01. Looking up in the standard normal table, the z-score for 0.99 (since 0.5 + 0.49) is 2.326. Yes, that's correct.

So the calculation steps:

1. Sample mean (x̄) = 23
2. Sample standard deviation (s) = 11.6
3. Sample size (n) = 70
4. Confidence level = 98%, so α = 0.02, α/2 = 0.01
5. z* = 2.326 (from standard normal table)
6. Standard error (SE) = s / sqrt(n) = 11.6 / sqrt(70) ≈ 11.6 / 8.3666 ≈ 1.386
